<p><b>Leonardo Bonucci</b> (<small>Italian pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Italian" title="Help:IPA/Italian">[leonardo bonutti]</a></span>; born 1 May 1987) is an Italian professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Centre-back" class="mw-redirect" title="Centre-back">centre-back</a> for and serves as vice captain of both <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> club <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy national team</a>.
</p><p>After beginning his career with <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a> in 2005, Bonucci spent the next few seasons on loan at <a href="/wiki/F.C._Treviso" class="mw-redirect" title="F.C. Treviso">Treviso</a> and <a href="/wiki/A.C._Pisa_1909" title="A.C. Pisa 1909">Pisa</a>, before moving to <a href="/wiki/A.S._Bari" class="mw-redirect" title="A.S. Bari">Bari</a> in 2009. His technique, ball-playing ability and defensive performances alongside fellow Italian centre-back <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Ranocchia" title="Andrea Ranocchia">Andrea Ranocchia</a> earned him a move to <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> the following season, where he later became a key member of the club's three-man defensive line, alongside <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Chiellini" title="Giorgio Chiellini">Giorgio Chiellini</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Barzagli" title="Andrea Barzagli">Andrea Barzagli</a>, establishing himself as one of the best defenders in world football. He went on to win six consecutive <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> titles with the team between 2012 and 2017. In 2017, he moved to <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">A.C. Milan</a>, and one season later returned to Juventus, winning two more consecutive league titles with the club.
</p><p>At international level, Bonucci has represented Italy at two <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a> (<a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014</a>), two <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Football_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA European Football Championships">European Championships</a> (2012 and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">2016</a>), and a <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="FIFA Confederations Cup">FIFA Confederations Cup</a> (2013), winning a runners-up medal at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">Euro 2012</a>, and a third-place medal at the <a href="/wiki/2013_FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="2013 FIFA Confederations Cup">2013 FIFA Confederations Cup</a>.
</p><p>Bonucci has also won several individual honours for his performances: he was named to the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> Squad of the season during the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Europa_League#Squad_of_the_season" title="2013–14 UEFA Europa League">2013–14</a> and <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_UEFA_Europa_League#Squad_of_the_season" title="2017–18 UEFA Europa League">2017–18</a> seasons, and is a three-time member of the <a href="/wiki/Serie_A_Team_of_the_Year" title="Serie A Team of the Year">Serie A Team of the Year</a>. He was named the <a href="/wiki/Serie_A_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="Serie A Footballer of the Year">Serie A Footballer of the Year</a> in 2016, and was also included in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="UEFA Team of the Year">UEFA Team of the Year</a> in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Team_of_the_Year#Team_of_the_Year_2016" title="UEFA Team of the Year">same season</a>. In <a href="/wiki/The_Best_FIFA_Football_Awards_2017#FIFA_FIFPro_World11" title="The Best FIFA Football Awards 2017">2017</a>, he was also included in the <a href="/wiki/FIFPro#FIFPro_World_XI" title="FIFPro">FIFA FIFPro World XI</a> and the <a href="/wiki/IFFHS_Men%27s_World_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="IFFHS Men&#39;s World Team">IFFHS Men's World Team</a>, as well as the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UEFA_Champions_League#Squad_of_the_season" title="2016–17 UEFA Champions League">2016–17</a> <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League Team of the Season</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Sports_Media#2010s" title="European Sports Media">2016–17</a> <a href="/wiki/European_Sports_Media#ESM_Team_of_the_Season" title="European Sports Media">ESM Team of the Year</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_Bonucci&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Club career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inter_Milan">Inter Milan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_Bonucci&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Inter Milan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bonucci started his career in the youth ranks of his hometown club <a href="/wiki/A.S._Viterbese_Calcio" class="mw-redirect" title="A.S. Viterbese Calcio">Viterbese</a> but was loaned to <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Inter Milan</a> in the summer of 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> He played a number of pre-season friendlies for the Inter first team.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> He then became a member of the Inter <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan_youth_teams" class="mw-redirect" title="Inter Milan youth teams">U20 team</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 May 2006, Bonucci made his <a href="/wiki/Serie_A" title="Serie A">Serie A</a> debut in the last match of the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Serie_A" title="2005–06 Serie A">2005–06 season</a>, in a 2–2 away draw against <a href="/wiki/Cagliari_Calcio" title="Cagliari Calcio">Cagliari</a>, which was Inter's 3,500th competitive match.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> On 7 July 2006, Inter bought Bonucci outright.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He played his first <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Coppa_Italia" title="2006–07 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> match against <a href="/wiki/F.C._Messina_Peloro" class="mw-redirect" title="F.C. Messina Peloro">Messina</a> on 9 November 2006 when he <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Substitute (football)">came off the bench for</a> <a href="/wiki/Fabio_Grosso" title="Fabio Grosso">Fabio Grosso</a> in the 86th minute. Bonucci featured in two more Coppa Italia games for Inter that season when he was brought on for the substituted <a href="/wiki/Walter_Samuel" title="Walter Samuel">Walter Samuel</a> at half-time during the quarter final second leg match against <a href="/wiki/Empoli_F.C." title="Empoli F.C.">Empoli</a>, and as a starter in the semi final second leg tie against <a href="/wiki/U.C._Sampdoria" title="U.C. Sampdoria">Sampdoria</a>.
</p><p>In January 2007, Inter sold 50% of Bonucci's registration rights to <a href="/wiki/Treviso_F.B.C._1993" class="mw-redirect" title="Treviso F.B.C. 1993">Treviso</a>, along with 50% of the registration rights for fellow Primavera team-mate <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Maa_Boumsong" title="Daniel Maa Boumsong">Daniel Maa Boumsong</a>. At that time Bonucci was tagged for a peppercorn fee of €500.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Bonucci subsequently remained at Inter until 30 June 2007<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> while Maa Boumsong returned from Treviso where he spent the first half of the season on loan. During Bonucci's last season with the Inter's youth side, he won the <a href="/wiki/Campionato_Nazionale_Primavera" title="Campionato Nazionale Primavera">Campionato Nazionale Primavera</a> (the national youth league title).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Treviso_and_Pisa">Treviso and Pisa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_Bonucci&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Treviso and Pisa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 1 July 2007, Bonucci and Maa Boumsong formally became players of Treviso after their loan contract back to Inter had expired, as well as the renewal of the co-ownerships in June 2007. At Treviso, Bonucci made 20 starts in 27 Serie B appearances as one of the regular starters.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2008, among the other Inter youth products, Bonucci was the only player that was bought back from Treviso.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> However, he was loaned back to Treviso for the 2008–09 season. According to a Treviso filing named <i>Tabella N°5 – circolare Co.Vi.So.C. prot. N°4051.4/GC/pc del 11 maggio 2005</i> in their 2007–08 financial report, Bonucci was sold for a €700,000 fee.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonucci played 13 Serie B matches for Treviso before leaving for another Serie B struggler <a href="/wiki/Pisa_Calcio" class="mw-redirect" title="Pisa Calcio">Pisa</a> on loan.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bari">Bari</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_Bonucci&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Bari">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leonardo_Bonucci_-_2009_-_AS_Bari.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Leonardo_Bonucci_-_2009_-_AS_Bari.png/190px-Leonardo_Bonucci_-_2009_-_AS_Bari.png" decoding="async" width="190" height="232" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Leonardo_Bonucci_-_2009_-_AS_Bari.png/285px-Leonardo_Bonucci_-_2009_-_AS_Bari.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Leonardo_Bonucci_-_2009_-_AS_Bari.png/380px-Leonardo_Bonucci_-_2009_-_AS_Bari.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="550" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leonardo_Bonucci_-_2009_-_AS_Bari.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonucci playing for <a href="/wiki/AS_Bari" class="mw-redirect" title="AS Bari">Bari</a> in the 2009–10 season</div></div></div>
<p>On 8 June 2009, Bonucci underwent a medical examination at <a href="/wiki/Genoa_C.F.C." title="Genoa C.F.C.">Genoa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> On 1 July, Inter officially announced that Bonucci,<sup id="cite_ref-Motta_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Motta-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> along with <a href="/wiki/Robert_Acquafresca" title="Robert Acquafresca">Acquafresca</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Milito_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Milito-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Bolzoni" title="Francesco Bolzoni">Bolzoni</a><sup id="cite_ref-Motta_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Motta-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Riccardo_Meggiorini" title="Riccardo Meggiorini">Meggiorini</a><sup id="cite_ref-Motta_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Motta-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> had been transferred to Genoa, as part of the deal that sent <a href="/wiki/Diego_Milito" title="Diego Milito">Diego Milito</a><sup id="cite_ref-Milito_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Milito-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Thiago_Motta" title="Thiago Motta">Thiago Motta</a><sup id="cite_ref-Motta_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Motta-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> to Inter. Moreover, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Fati%C4%87" title="Ivan Fati">Ivan Fati</a> who was co-contracted ("co-owned") between Chievo and Inter, became co-contracted between Chievo and Genoa instead, according to a news article by <i><a href="/wiki/La_Gazzetta_dello_Sport" title="La Gazzetta dello Sport">La Gazzetta dello Sport</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Bonucci was valued at €3&#160;million at that time.<sup id="cite_ref-Genoa2009bilancio_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Genoa2009bilancio-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 July he was transferred to <a href="/wiki/A.S._Bari" class="mw-redirect" title="A.S. Bari">Bari</a> from Genoa, on a co-ownership deal, for €1.75 million,<sup id="cite_ref-Genoa2009bilancio_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Genoa2009bilancio-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> along with Meggiorini (also on a co-ownership deal), <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Paro" title="Matteo Paro">Matteo Paro</a> (on loan), <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Ranocchia" title="Andrea Ranocchia">Andrea Ranocchia</a> (on loan) and <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Greco_(footballer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Giuseppe Greco (footballer)">Giuseppe Greco</a> (on loan).
</p><p>At Bari he became a first team player in central defence under head coach <a href="/wiki/Gian_Piero_Ventura" title="Gian Piero Ventura">Gian Piero Ventura</a>, showing a composed yet strong and effective defensive playing style. He formed an extremely strong defensive partnership with Andrea Ranocchia which was so effective that, as of the midway point in the 2009–10 season, Bari had the second best defensive record in Serie A. The strong partnership ended after Ranocchia got injured half-way through the season and was ruled out for the remaining fixtures.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Juventus">Juventus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_Bonucci&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Juventus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 1 July 2010, Bonucci was signed by <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> on a four-year contract for a total of €15.5 million fee<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> from Bari; Bari bought Bonucci from Genoa outright for €8&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> However, Genoa and Bari used part of the transfer <a href="/wiki/Receivable" class="mw-redirect" title="Receivable">receivables</a> to sign the remaining 50% registration rights of <a href="/wiki/Domenico_Criscito" title="Domenico Criscito">Domenico Criscito</a><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and 50% of the registration rights of <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Bernardo_Almir%C3%B3n" title="Sergio Bernardo Almirón">Sergio Bernardo Almirón</a> from Juventus.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Bonucci was assigned the shirt number 19.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Partnered with Italy teammate <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Chiellini" title="Giorgio Chiellini">Giorgio Chiellini</a> in defence, Bonucci was immediately drafted into the starting line-up for the first matches of the season. He scored his first goal for Juventus in the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_UEFA_Europa_League_qualifying_phase_and_play-off_round#Sturm_Graz_v_Juventus" class="mw-redirect" title="2010–11 UEFA Europa League qualifying phase and play-off round">Europa League play-off</a> match against <a href="/wiki/SK_Sturm_Graz" title="SK Sturm Graz">Sturm Graz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The following season, due to the presence of veteran of <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Barzagli" title="Andrea Barzagli">Andrea Barzagli</a>, it was expected that Bonucci would compete with him for a starting place alongside Chiellini in a four-man defence, as the club's new manager <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Conte" title="Antonio Conte">Antonio Conte</a> was known for his preference for the 4–2–4 formation, a variant upon the 4–4–2 formation. However, after experimenting with several tactical systems, Conte eventually decided to play all three players in a three-man defence aided by <a href="/wiki/Defender_(association_football)#Wing-back" title="Defender (association football)">wingbacks</a> in a 3–5–2 formation, and Bonucci established himself once again in the starting eleven alongside Chiellini and Barzagli.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Due to their performances together, the three-man defence earned the nickname <i>BBC</i>, a reference to the players' initials.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Soon, the trio established themselves as one of the best defences in world football during the following seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-opposition_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opposition-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> On 2 April 2012 Juventus announced that he had signed a new 5-year contract<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> effective on 1 July 2012. Bonucci won his first major title, the 2011–12 <i><a href="/wiki/Scudetto" title="Scudetto">Scudetto</a></i>, and contributed two goals as Juventus finished the season undefeated and with one of the best defensive records in the top five <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">European</a> leagues. His good form that season earned him a place in the final <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a> squad.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_Selection_vs_Juventus_-_2014_-_Leonardo_Bonucci.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Singapore_Selection_vs_Juventus_-_2014_-_Leonardo_Bonucci.jpg/190px-Singapore_Selection_vs_Juventus_-_2014_-_Leonardo_Bonucci.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="280" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Singapore_Selection_vs_Juventus_-_2014_-_Leonardo_Bonucci.jpg/285px-Singapore_Selection_vs_Juventus_-_2014_-_Leonardo_Bonucci.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Singapore_Selection_vs_Juventus_-_2014_-_Leonardo_Bonucci.jpg/380px-Singapore_Selection_vs_Juventus_-_2014_-_Leonardo_Bonucci.jpg 2x" data-file-width="888" data-file-height="1310" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Singapore_Selection_vs_Juventus_-_2014_-_Leonardo_Bonucci.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonucci playing for <a href="/wiki/Juventus_F.C." title="Juventus F.C.">Juventus</a> in 2014</div></div></div>
<p>Bonucci began the season by winning the <a href="/wiki/2012_Supercoppa_Italiana" title="2012 Supercoppa Italiana">2012 Supercoppa Italiana</a> with Juventus. He made his <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2012–13 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> debut against <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage#Group_E" title="2012–13 UEFA Champions League group stage">group stage</a> and scored his first goal in the competition against <a href="/wiki/Shaktar_Donetsk" class="mw-redirect" title="Shaktar Donetsk">Shaktar Donetsk</a> on October 2012 in a 1–1 draw.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> On December 2012 Bonucci was criticized for diving in a league game against Palermo on which was described by a number of journalists as "the worst dive ever".<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> He was <a href="/wiki/Penalty_card#Yellow_card" title="Penalty card">booked</a> by the referee during the game and subsequently given a one-match ban and a €2000 fine by the authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Juventus finished the season by winning the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Serie_A" title="2012–13 Serie A">2012–13 Serie A</a> title.
</p><p>The following season, Bonucci would help Juventus to defend the <a href="/wiki/2013_Supercoppa_Italiana" title="2013 Supercoppa Italiana">Supercoppa Italiana</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Serie_A" title="2013–14 Serie A">Serie A title</a>, although Juventus would suffer a group-stage elimination in the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>. Nevertheless, he helped Juventus to reach the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2013–14 UEFA Europa League">Europa League</a>, scoring a decisive goal against <a href="/wiki/Olympique_Lyonnais" title="Olympique Lyonnais">Lyon</a> in the quarter-finals.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Serie_A" title="2014–15 Serie A">2014–15 season</a>, Bonucci made his 200th appearance with Juventus on 25 January 2015, in a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/A.C._ChievoVerona" title="A.C. ChievoVerona">Chievo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> On 6 June 2015, Bonucci started for Juventus in the <a href="/wiki/2015_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2015 UEFA Champions League Final">2015 UEFA Champions League Final</a>, but were defeated 3–1 by <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a> at Berlin's <a href="/wiki/Olympiastadion_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympiastadion Berlin">Olympiastadion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> With 52 appearances, he made the most appearances for Juventus that season across all competitions, along with team-mates <a href="/wiki/Claudio_Marchisio" title="Claudio Marchisio">Claudio Marchisio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Pereyra" title="Roberto Pereyra">Roberto Pereyra</a>. On 24 November 2015, Bonucci was nominated for the 2015 UEFA Team of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> On 2 March 2016, he captained Juventus in the absence of <a href="/wiki/Gianluigi_Buffon" title="Gianluigi Buffon">Gianluigi Buffon</a> and Chiellini, scoring the decisive penalty in the resulting shoot-out of the second leg of the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Coppa_Italia" title="2015–16 Coppa Italia">Coppa Italia</a> semi-finals against Inter, at the <a href="/wiki/San_Siro" title="San Siro">San Siro</a>, following a 3–3 draw on aggregate, which allowed Juventus to progress to the <a href="/wiki/2016_Coppa_Italia_Final" title="2016 Coppa Italia Final">final</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> however, due to the yellow card he received during the match, and having already been booked prior to the fixture, he missed the victorious final against Milan, which saw Juventus capture a domestic double for the second consecutive season,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> including a record fifth consecutive league title.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Serie_A" title="2016–17 Serie A">2016–17 season</a>, Bonucci dedicated time to his ill son Matteo, missing select matches with Juventus and the national team.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> On 27 November, Bonucci suffered a severe thigh strain in an eventual 3–1 away loss to Genoa, sidelining him for up to 60 days.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> On 19 December, Bonucci penned a new deal with Juventus, keeping him at the club until 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> On 5 January 2017, Bonucci was named to the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Team_of_the_Year#Team_of_the_Year_2016" title="UEFA Team of the Year">2016 UEFA Team of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UEFATeamOTY2016_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UEFATeamOTY2016-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> On 30 January, Bonucci was named to the <a href="/wiki/Serie_A_Team_of_the_Year#2015.E2.80.9316" title="Serie A Team of the Year">2015–16 Serie A Team of the Year</a>, and was also named the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Serie_A_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="Serie A Footballer of the Year">Serie A Footballer of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gran_Galà_del_calcio_-_2016_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gran_Galà_del_calcio_-_2016-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Bonucci made his 300th Juventus appearance in a 4–1 home win over Palermo on 17 February;<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> however, after Palermo scored a late goal, Bonucci had an argument on the touchline with coach <a href="/wiki/Massimiliano_Allegri" title="Massimiliano Allegri">Massimiliano Allegri</a>, causing the club to fine and omit him from the squad for the first <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2016–17 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> round of 16 leg with <a href="/wiki/FC_Porto" title="FC Porto">Porto</a> on 22 February.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> On 17 May, Bonucci scored the last goal of a 2–0 win in the <a href="/wiki/2017_Coppa_Italia_Final" title="2017 Coppa Italia Final">final</a> of the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Coppa_Italia" title="2016–17 Coppa Italia">2016–17 Coppa Italia</a> over <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio" title="S.S. Lazio">Lazio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> On 3 June, Bonucci started in his <a href="/wiki/2017_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2017 UEFA Champions League Final">second Champions League Final</a> in three years, but Juventus were defeated 4–1 by defending champions <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_CF" title="Real Madrid CF">Real Madrid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> On 5 June, he was subsequently named to the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UEFA_Champions_League#Squad_of_the_season" title="2016–17 UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League squad of the season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UEFA_Champions_League_squad_of_the_season_2017_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UEFA_Champions_League_squad_of_the_season_2017-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Milan">Milan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_Bonucci&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Milan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 14 July 2017, Bonucci was signed by <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">A.C. Milan</a> on a five-year contract for a €42 million fee.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> On 4 August 2017, Bonucci was named one of the three finalists for the Defender of the 2016–17 UEFA Champions League season award.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Milan's manager <a href="/wiki/Vincenzo_Montella" title="Vincenzo Montella">Vincenzo Montella</a> subsequently named Bonucci as the team's new captain later that month.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> On 23 October, he was named to the <a href="/wiki/The_Best_FIFA_Football_Awards_2017#FIFA_FIFPro_World11" title="The Best FIFA Football Awards 2017">2017 FIFA FIFPro World11</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FIFPRO-WORLDXI2017_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FIFPRO-WORLDXI2017-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Although much was expected of Bonucci and Milan, the first half of the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_A.C._Milan_season" title="2017–18 A.C. Milan season">2017–18 season</a> was disappointing both for him and the club, and he drew criticism in the media over the quality of his performances.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first goal for Milan on 6 January 2018, in a 1–0 home win over <a href="/wiki/F.C._Crotone" title="F.C. Crotone">Crotone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> On 31 March, Bonucci scored the equalising goal against his former team away to Juventus, breaking goalkeeper Gianluigi Buffon's <a href="/wiki/Football_records_and_statistics_in_Italy#Goalkeeping" title="Football records and statistics in Italy">record of longest consecutive minutes not conceded</a> in an eventual 3–1 defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_Juventus">Return to Juventus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_Bonucci&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Return to Juventus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 2 August 2018, Bonucci returned to Juventus as part of a swap deal with <a href="/wiki/A.C._Milan" title="A.C. Milan">A.C. Milan</a> involving <a href="/wiki/Mattia_Caldara" title="Mattia Caldara">Mattia Caldara</a>; both Bonucci and Caldara were tagged for €35&#160;million transfer fee. He signed a five-year contract until 30 June 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Bonucci made his return for Juventus in their opening Serie A match on 18 August, a 3–2 away win over <a href="/wiki/A.C._ChievoVerona" title="A.C. ChievoVerona">Chievo</a>, contributing to Juventus's temporary equaliser, an own goal by <a href="/wiki/Mattia_Bani" title="Mattia Bani">Mattia Bani</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> On 29 September 2018, Bonucci scored his first goal for Juventus since his return from Milan, the final goal of a 3–1 home win over <a href="/wiki/S.S.C._Napoli" title="S.S.C. Napoli">Napoli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> On 2 October, he made his 50th <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2018–19 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> appearance in a 3–0 home win over <a href="/wiki/BSC_Young_Boys" title="BSC Young Boys">Young Boys</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> On 2 April 2019, Bonucci marked his 250th Serie A appearance with Juventus by scoring the opening goal in a 2–0 away win against Cagliari.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> However, following the match, he was heavily criticised by several prominent figures after stating that teammate <a href="/wiki/Moise_Kean" title="Moise Kean">Moise Kean</a> was partly to blame for the racial abuse he suffered from the crowd;<sup id="cite_ref-auto_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> England international <a href="/wiki/Raheem_Sterling" title="Raheem Sterling">Raheem Sterling</a> deemed the comments 'laughable',<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> while compatriot <a href="/wiki/Mario_Balotelli" title="Mario Balotelli">Mario Balotelli</a>, English singer <a href="/wiki/Stormzy" title="Stormzy">Stormzy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> and former Juventus player <a href="/wiki/Paul_Pogba" title="Paul Pogba">Paul Pogba</a> also criticised Bonucci's comments.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Bonucci implied that Kean's goal celebration caused further jeers, stating to <a href="/wiki/Sky_Sport_(Italy)" title="Sky Sport (Italy)">Sky Sport Italia</a>: "Kean knows that when he scores a goal, he has to focus on celebrating with his teammates. He knows he could've done something differently too. There were racist jeers after the goal, <a href="/wiki/Blaise_Matuidi" title="Blaise Matuidi">Blaise</a> heard it and was angered. I think the blame is 50–50, because Moise shouldn't have done that and the Curva should not have reacted that way. We are professionals, we have to set the example and not provoke anyone." Later, he made a post on <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> which read "Regardless of everything, in any case... no to racism."<sup id="cite_ref-auto_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In response to the criticism, the following day, Bonucci posted on Instagram: "After 24 hours I want to clarify my feelings. Yesterday I was interviewed right at the end of the game, and my words have been clearly misunderstood, probably because I was too hasty in the way I expressed my thoughts. Hours and years wouldn't be enough to talk about this topic. I firmly condemn all forms of racism and discrimination. The abuses are not acceptable at all and this must not be misunderstood."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After Chiellini suffered an <a href="/wiki/Anterior_cruciate_ligament_injury" title="Anterior cruciate ligament injury">anterior cruciate ligament injury</a> at the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Juventus_F.C._season" title="2019–20 Juventus F.C. season">2019–20 season</a>, Bonucci captained Juventus in his absence.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In November 2019, he signed a new contract with the club, running until 2024.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 September 2020, Bonucci scored in Juventus's opening match of the season, a 3–0 home win over Sampdoria in Serie A.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_Bonucci&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: International career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>At youth level, Bonucci played for the <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_under-21_football_B_team" title="Italy national under-21 football B team">Italy national under-21 football B team</a>. He was called-up for a friendlies against <a href="/wiki/A.C._Renate" title="A.C. Renate">Renate</a> on 6 November 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> and against the <a href="/wiki/Italy_Lega_Pro_representative_teams" class="mw-redirect" title="Italy Lega Pro representative teams">Under-20 Serie C representative team</a> on 4 December 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> He was also capped for the team in an internal friendly, which split the Under-21 Serie B team into two on 9 October 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> on 21 October 2008,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> on 25 November,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> and on 24 March 2009, as team captain.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He also received a call-up from the <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_under-20_football_team" title="Italy national under-20 football team">Italy U20 team</a> on 31 May 2007. He was an unused substitute in the 0–1 loss to the Serie D Best XI.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonucci made his debut with the <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy senior team</a> on 3 March 2010, under manager <a href="/wiki/Marcello_Lippi" title="Marcello Lippi">Marcello Lippi</a>, in a friendly match against <a href="/wiki/Cameroon_national_football_team" title="Cameroon national football team">Cameroon</a> played in <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, which ended in a 0–0 draw,<sup id="cite_ref-Nazionale_in_cifre:_Bonucci,_Leonardo_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nazionale_in_cifre:_Bonucci,_Leonardo-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> and became one of the few debutants to have never played an official match for the national youth teams.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> He was included by manager Marcello Lippi in the starting line-up along with national team regulars <a href="/wiki/Fabio_Cannavaro" title="Fabio Cannavaro">Fabio Cannavaro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Chiellini" title="Giorgio Chiellini">Giorgio Chiellini</a>, forming a three-man defensive line in Lippi's 3–4–3 formation.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leonardo_Bonucci_and_Cesc_F%C3%A0bregas_Euro_2012_final.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Leonardo_Bonucci_and_Cesc_F%C3%A0bregas_Euro_2012_final.jpg/220px-Leonardo_Bonucci_and_Cesc_F%C3%A0bregas_Euro_2012_final.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Leonardo_Bonucci_and_Cesc_F%C3%A0bregas_Euro_2012_final.jpg/330px-Leonardo_Bonucci_and_Cesc_F%C3%A0bregas_Euro_2012_final.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Leonardo_Bonucci_and_Cesc_F%C3%A0bregas_Euro_2012_final.jpg/440px-Leonardo_Bonucci_and_Cesc_F%C3%A0bregas_Euro_2012_final.jpg 2x" data-file-width="656" data-file-height="435" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leonardo_Bonucci_and_Cesc_F%C3%A0bregas_Euro_2012_final.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bonucci (right) playing against <a href="/wiki/Cesc_F%C3%A0bregas" title="Cesc Fàbregas">Cesc Fàbregas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a> in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012_Final" title="UEFA Euro 2012 Final">UEFA Euro 2012 Final</a></div></div></div>
<p>Due to his performances during the 2009–10 season, Bonucci was included in the Italy squad for the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> He scored his first international goal on 3 June 2010, in a 1–2 friendly loss against <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a>, in a pre-tournament friendly match in Brussels.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> In the World Cup, he appeared as an unused substitute for all three of Italy's matches, as they suffered a first-round elimination, failing to win a match.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonucci ended a fine 2011–12 season by earning a place in the final 23-man Italy squad for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a>, under manager <a href="/wiki/Cesare_Prandelli" title="Cesare Prandelli">Cesare Prandelli</a>, helping Italy to reach the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012_Final" title="UEFA Euro 2012 Final">final</a> of the tournament, where they were defeated 4–0 by defending champions <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> He started in all but one match as Italy reached the finals.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2013_FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="2013 FIFA Confederations Cup">2013 FIFA Confederations Cup</a> he missed his spot-kick in the penalty shoot-out against <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2013_FIFA_Confederations_Cup_knockout_stage" title="2013 FIFA Confederations Cup knockout stage">semi-finals</a>, shooting high over the bar as Italy went out of the competition losing 7–6 on penalties;<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Italy would win the bronze medal match over <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_national_football_team" title="Uruguay national football team">Uruguay</a> 4–3 on penalties, after a 2–2 draw following extra-time, allowing them to capture third place.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonucci was selected by Cesare Prandelli to be part of the Italy squad that would take part at the <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a> in Brazil. Although he once again remained an unused substitute for the first two games, he made his World Cup debut on 24 June 2014, in a 0–1 loss to Uruguay; as a result, Italy was eliminated in the first round of the competition for a second consecutive time.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 4 September 2014, under new Italy manager <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Conte" title="Antonio Conte">Antonio Conte</a>, Bonucci wore the <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captain</a>'s armband for Italy for the first time, following <a href="/wiki/Daniele_De_Rossi" title="Daniele De Rossi">Daniele De Rossi</a>'s substitution in a 2–0 friendly win over the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 31 May 2016, Bonucci was named to Conte's 23-man Italy squad for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> On 13 June he set up <a href="/wiki/Emanuele_Giaccherini" title="Emanuele Giaccherini">Emanuele Giaccherini</a>'s goal, Italy's first of the match, with a long ball in a 2–0 win over <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a> in the opening group match of Euro 2016; he was later booked for a tactical foul.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> After helping Italy to another clean-sheet in a 1–0 victory in the second group match against <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a> on 17 June, Bonucci was once again praised for his defensive performances alongside Chiellini and Barzagli.<sup id="cite_ref-opposition_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opposition-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> On 22 June, he captained Italy in Buffon's absence in his nation's final group match, a 1–0 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> On 27 June he produced a <i>Man of the Match</i> performance in the round of 16 of the tournament as he helped Italy to keep a third clean sheet and defeat defending champions Spain 2–0.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In the quarter-final fixture against <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> on 2 July, he scored Italy's equalising goal from a penalty, although his spot-kick was saved by <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Neuer" title="Manuel Neuer">Manuel Neuer</a> in the resulting shoot-out, as the reigning World Cup champions advanced to the semi-finals following a 6–5 shoot-out victory.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">2018 FIFA World Cup qualifying</a> campaign Italy finished in second place in Group G behind Spain and advanced to the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Second_Round#Matches" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Second Round">play-off</a> against <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a>. Italy failed to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a> after a 1–0 aggregate loss to the Scandinavians.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 12 October 2019, Bonucci made his 92nd international appearance, under manager <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Mancini" title="Roberto Mancini">Roberto Mancini</a>, in a 2–0 home win over <a href="/wiki/Greece_national_football_team" title="Greece national football team">Greece</a>, and overtook <a href="/wiki/Alessandro_Del_Piero" title="Alessandro Del Piero">Alessandro Del Piero</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team_records_and_statistics#Appearances" title="Italy national football team records and statistics">tenth-most capped player in the history of the Italian national team</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> the victory sealed Italy's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2020 qualifying">qualification</a> for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020" title="UEFA Euro 2020">Euro 2020</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> He made his 94th appearance for Italy on 15 November, in a 3–0 away win over <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_national_football_team" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina national football team">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, in a Euro 2020 qualifier, equalling <a href="/wiki/Giacinto_Facchetti" title="Giacinto Facchetti">Giacinto Facchetti</a> as the ninth most-capped Italian player of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>On 11 October 2020, Bonucci made his 98th international appearance in a 0–0 away draw against <a href="/wiki/Poland_national_football_team" title="Poland national football team">Poland</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_UEFA_Nations_League" title="2020–21 UEFA Nations League">UEFA Nations League</a>, equalling <a href="/wiki/Gianluca_Zambrotta" title="Gianluca Zambrotta">Gianluca Zambrotta</a> as the eight–most capped player of all–time for the Italian national team.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_Bonucci&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Style of play">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>A former midfielder who is usually deployed as ball-playing <a href="/wiki/Centre-back" class="mw-redirect" title="Centre-back">centre-back</a> in a three-man defence<sup id="cite_ref-Ferrari_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferrari-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Italy’s_World_Cup_23_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Italy’s_World_Cup_23-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> (although he is also capable of playing in a four-man defence, both in the centre or <a href="/wiki/Defender_(association_football)#Full-back" title="Defender (association football)">out wide</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-Italy’s_World_Cup_23_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Italy’s_World_Cup_23-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leader_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leader-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-regret_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regret-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Bonucci is primarily known for his technique, passing range, and his ability to <a href="/wiki/Playmaker#Playmaking_in_other_positions" title="Playmaker">launch an attack from the back</a> with <a href="/wiki/Long_ball" title="Long ball">long passes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferrari_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferrari-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Italy’s_World_Cup_23_121-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Italy’s_World_Cup_23-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Although he is not the quickest player over short distances, he is a tall, mobile, and strong defender, with a good positional sense, as well as good anticipation, solid tackling, and an ability to read the game and mark opponents, on top of his ball skills; he also excels in the air, and frequently poses a goal threat from set pieces.<sup id="cite_ref-Italy’s_World_Cup_23_121-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Italy’s_World_Cup_23-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leader_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leader-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-regret_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regret-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bonucci_e_la_classifica_degli_8_migliori_difensori_italiani_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bonucci_e_la_classifica_degli_8_migliori_difensori_italiani-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Although he was considered to be a talented and promising young defender,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> he was also criticised by certain pundits for being inconsistent and prone to errors or lapses in concentration in his youth, which were dubbed "Bonucciate" in the Italian media;<sup id="cite_ref-Italy’s_World_Cup_23_121-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Italy’s_World_Cup_23-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leader_123-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leader-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> however, he showed notable improvements during the 2014–15 season, and established himself as one of the best defenders in world football, also drawing praise from manager <a href="/wiki/Pep_Guardiola" title="Pep Guardiola">Pep Guardiola</a>, who described Bonucci as one of his "favourite ever players".<sup id="cite_ref-Ferrari_120-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferrari-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leader_123-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leader-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-regret_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-regret-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bonucci_e_la_classifica_degli_8_migliori_difensori_italiani_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bonucci_e_la_classifica_degli_8_migliori_difensori_italiani-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-improved_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-improved-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, Mario Sconcerti of <i><a href="/wiki/Il_Corriere_della_Sera" class="mw-redirect" title="Il Corriere della Sera">Il Corriere della Sera</a></i> ranked Bonucci among the greatest Italian defenders of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-Bonucci_e_la_classifica_degli_8_migliori_difensori_italiani_126-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bonucci_e_la_classifica_degli_8_migliori_difensori_italiani-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> His unique playing style has led <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Galli" title="Giovanni Galli">Giovanni Galli</a> to compare him to former <a href="/wiki/Sweeper_(association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sweeper (association football)">sweeper</a> <a href="/wiki/Gaetano_Scirea" title="Gaetano Scirea">Gaetano Scirea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ferrari_120-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferrari-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian_(newspaper)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Guardian (newspaper)">The Guardian</a></i> named him the 88th Best Player in the World<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> and in 2016, he was named the 26th Best Player in the World.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, his defensive attributes, as well as his skill on the ball, vision, and accurate passing, moved <i><a href="/wiki/La_Repubblica" title="La Repubblica">La Repubblica</a></i> to dub him as “Beckenbonucci”, a reference to former German sweeper <a href="/wiki/Franz_Beckenbauer" title="Franz Beckenbauer">Franz Beckenbauer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-spotlight_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spotlight-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> In addition to his defensive, playmaking and technical skills, Bonucci has also been praised for his leadership and ability to organise his back-line.<sup id="cite_ref-Italy’s_World_Cup_23_121-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Italy’s_World_Cup_23-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-leader_123-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leader-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, he was ranked by some as the best defender in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_Bonucci&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 18 June 2011, Bonucci married Martina Maccari (b. 19 November 1985),<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> a former model and blogger, whom she first met in 2008 through a mutual friend.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> They have two sons, Lorenzo (b. July 2012)<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> and Matteo (b. May 2014), and one daughter, Matilda (b. February 2019).<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Although Bonucci played for Juventus for several seasons, his eldest son, Lorenzo, supports Juventus's <a href="/wiki/Derby_della_Mole" title="Derby della Mole">cross-city rivals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Torino_F.C." title="Torino F.C.">Torino</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> In July 2016, Bonucci's youngest son, Matteo underwent emergency surgery following the onset of an acute illness.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> In a 2017 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/El_Pa%C3%ADs" title="El País">El País</a></i>, Bonucci revealed that his son's illness had even led him to think about quitting football, commenting:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"For three or four months, my head was just not in the right place, it’s the head that gets the legs moving. For around 15 days after the surgery, until I started to see him improving, I was just not interested in training or anything to do with football. I've always hated hospitals and tried to avoid them, but at that time I had to be there and I was really struggling to be calm. Matteo is much better now and our family feels more united than ever. Yes, I thought about quitting. Football was just not my priority at that moment. You see your son with so much to live for, he’s asking you so many questions and why this is happening to him... and I had no answers. Priorities change at those times. Now I tell myself that I am lucky. Everything I have done has been from the heart."<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Bonucci's older brother, Riccardo (b. November 1982), was also a footballer who once played as a central defender in <a href="/wiki/Serie_C1" class="mw-redirect" title="Serie C1">Serie C1</a> with Viterbese.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Their father owns a paint shop in <a href="/wiki/Viterbo" title="Viterbo">Viterbo</a>.
</p><p>In May 2012, during the <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Italian_football_scandal" class="mw-redirect" title="2011–12 Italian football scandal">2011–12 Italian football scandal</a> investigations, Bonucci, along with Juventus teammate <a href="/wiki/Simone_Pepe" title="Simone Pepe">Simone Pepe</a> and manager Antonio Conte, as well as many other players, were accused of match-fixing; Bonucci was accused of helping to fix the result of a 3–3 draw against <a href="/wiki/Udinese_Calcio" title="Udinese Calcio">Udinese</a> in May 2010, during his time with Bari, and faced a potential three-and-a-half year ban if found guilty. Bonucci denied any wrongdoing, however,<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> and both he and Pepe were later acquitted in August later that year.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2012, Bonucci and his wife and then five-month-old son were confronted by an armed robber who demanded the defender hand over his watch. As the robber reached out to take the watch, Bonucci reportedly punched him and chased him down the street. The robber escaped with his accomplice on a motorbike.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bonucci is an <a href="/wiki/Bullying" title="Bullying">anti-bullying</a> activist. In December 2017, he made a <a href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance" title="Cameo appearance">cameo appearance</a> in the music video for "Buona fortuna" by <a href="/wiki/Benji_%26_Fede" class="mw-redirect" title="Benji &amp; Fede">Benji &amp; Fede</a>, whose storyline deals with bullying.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> In October 2019, together with the journalist and editor Francesco Ceniti, he co-wrote and released a book "Il mio amico Leo", partially inspired by his own experiences and designed to provide support to bullying victims.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_statistics">Career statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_Bonucci&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Career statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Club">Club</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_Bonucci&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Club">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honours">Honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_Bonucci&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
